    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">

Matthea Harvey is the author of "Modern Life," a finalist for the National Book Critics Circle Award and a New York Times Notable Book. She teaches at Sarah Lawrence College and is a contributing editor to jubilat, Meatpaper and BOMB.

    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2013/07/wednesday-on-the-newshour-poet-liao-yiwu.html">Wednesday on the NewsHour: Poet Liao Yiwu</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>July 10, 2013</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Liao Yiwu was in his early 30s when he was arrested for writing and performing a poem about the brutality of the Tiananmen Square Massacre in 1989. A new memoir about his time in prison called "For a Song and A Hundred Songs" has just been published.

       </div>
    </div>

By Liao Yiwu, Translated by Wenguang Huang (Composed on the morning of June 4, 1989) Dedicated to those who were killed on June 4, 1989 Dedicated to the 200th anniversary of the French Revolution Leap! Howl! Fly! Run! Freedom feels...

Here, for the 4th of July, are Walt Whitman's lines:

    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2013/06/conversation-novelist-colum-mccann-author-of-transatlantic.html">Conversation: Novelist Colum McCann, Author of 'TransAtlantic'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>June 21, 2013</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Frederick Douglass traveling through Ireland in 1845 to stir up support for his abolitionist cause. The first non-stop flight across the Atlantic in 1919. Sen. George Mitchell in 1998 trying to forge a peace treaty in Northern Ireland. Those actual people and events are at the heart of a fictional story in the new novel "TransAtlantic" by author Colum McCann.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2013/06/pulling-back-the-burka-a-glimpse-of-afghan-life-through-poetry.html">Pulling Back the Burka: A Glimpse of Afghan Life Through Poetry</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>June 18, 2013</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Journalist and poet Eliza Griswold set out to document Afghan life through the prism of  oral folk poems shared mostly among Pashtun women. Seamus Murphy, the London-based photographer and filmmaker who worked with Griswold on the landay project, narrates a slideshow of some of his favorite images.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2013/06/weekly-poem-from-the-grandiloquent-dictionary.html">Weekly Poem: 'From the Grandiloquent Dictionary'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>June 17, 2013</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Hailey Leithauser's poetry has appeared in the Gettysburg Review, Poetry and in the Best American Poetry and Best New Poets anthologies. Her first book, "Swoop," won the Poetry Foundation's Emily Dickinson First Book Award. That collection will be published in October.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2013/06/thursday-on-the-newshour-walter-mosley.html">Thursday on the NewsHour: Novelist Walter Mosley</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>June 13, 2013</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Author Walter Mosley has written more than 40 books. His new mystery novel, "Little Green," revives one of the best-known, longest-running characters in American literature. Ezekiel "Easy" Rawlins, Mosley's fictional private eye, was last seen driving off a cliff.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2013/06/hit-the-road-poet-laureate-trethewey-partners-with-newshour-for-second-term.html">Hit the Road, Poet Laureate: Trethewey Partners With NewsHour for Second Term</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>June 10, 2013</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
The Library of Congress reappointed U.S. Poet Laureate Natasha Trethewey to a second term on Monday. Though she is not the first in her position to receive the honor of an extended post, the announcement does have special meaning for us at the PBS NewsHour.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2013/06/weekly-poem-charles-hood-reads-skype.html">Weekly Poem: Charles Hood Reads 'Skype'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>June 10, 2013</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Charles Hood is the author of "South x South" (Ohio University Press), winner of the 2012 Hollis Summers Poetry Prize. His previous books include "Bombing Ploesti" and "Rio de Dios" (Red Hen Press). He has been the recipient of a Fulbright fellowship, an Artist in Residency with the Center for Land Use Interpretation, and an Artists and Writers grant from the National Science Foundation. He teaches photography and writing at Antelope Valley College, Calif.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2013/06/charles-hood-is-the-author.html">Weekly Poem: Charles Hood Reads 'FSA'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">

      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>September 28, 2012</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;

    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>September 21, 2012</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
The new official face of American poetry is one familiar to NewsHour viewers. Natasha Trethewey has just taken on the job of poet laureate of the United States, appointed by the Librarian of Congress. She's the author of four books of verse, including the Pulitzer Prize-winning "Native Guard" and her latest, "Thrall."

       </div>

      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>May 16, 2012</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;

      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>December  2, 2011</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;

Eric Gudas":http://www.ericgudas.com/ was born in Annapolis, Md. His poems, book reviews and interviews with American poets have appeared in the American Poetry Review, Crazyhorse, the Iowa Review, Poetry Flash, the Southern Review and other journals. His book, "Best Western and Other Poems," winner of the 2008 Gerald Cable Book Award, was published in 2010 by "Silverfish Review Press":http://www.silverfishreviewpress.com/. He and his wife, Alyssa Sherwood, live with their daughter in Los Angeles, where he is completing a book about the life and writing of contemporary American poet Eleanor Ross Taylor.

       </div>
    </div>

The image of poetry fans gathered in a pub enjoying bagpipes, haggis, drinks and verse is a very Scottish one, but Scotland's national poet Robert Burns has fans worldwide who know there's no better way to honor the man and his writing.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2009/01/weekly-poem-a-mans-a-man-for-a-that.html">Weekly Poem: 'A Man's A Man for A' That'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>January 26, 2009</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
A Man's A Man for A' That by Robert Burns. Is there for honest Poverty That hings his head, an' a' that; The coward slave-we pass him by, We dare be poor for a' that!

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2009/01/conversation-roberto-bolanos-2666.html">Conversation: Roberto Bolano's '2666'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>January 23, 2009</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
For most of the English-speaking world and certainly for this reader, Roberto Bolano was unknown only a few years ago. Since then, he's become a literary phenomenon--his novels read, reviewed, discussed, widely praised.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2009/01/weekly-poem-title-of-poem-goes-here.html">Weekly Poem: 'Praise Song for the Day'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>January 20, 2009</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Praise Song for the Day by Elizabeth Alexander. Each day we go about our business, walking past each other, catching each other's eyes or not, about to speak or speaking.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2009/01/dodge-foundation-cancels-poetry-festival.html">Dodge Foundation Cancels Poetry Festival</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>January 16, 2009</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
The largest poetry festival in North America has just become the latest victim of the financial crisis. The Geraldine R. Dodge Foundation announced Friday in a letter to supporters that it will cancel the next Dodge Poetry Festival.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2009/01/weekly-poem-rose-hips.html">Weekly Poem: 'Rose Hips'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>January 12, 2009</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Sean Norton is the author of the book of poems, "Bad With Faces," from Red Morning Press. He lives in Ann Arbor, Mich., where he is the Assistant Director of the University of Michigan's Graduate Creative Writing Program.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2009/01/urban-iran-helps-lift-the-veil.html">'Urban Iran' Helps Lift the Veil</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>January  8, 2009</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
"What we are experiencing now is a re-emergence of art in Iran," writes photographer Sina Araghi in "Urban Iran," a collection of essays, photography, art and illustrations from Iranian artists in Tehran and abroad.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2009/01/weekly-poem-american-sublime.html">Weekly Poem: 'American Sublime'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>January  5, 2009</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Elizabeth Alexander will become just the fourth poet to recite a poem at a president's swearing-in ceremony on Jan. 20 at President-elect Barack Obama's inauguration.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2008/12/conversation-peter-matthiessen.html">Conversation: Peter Matthiessen</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>December 31, 2008</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Peter Matthiessen, a 2008 National Book Award winner, is best known as both a novelist and non-fiction writer, but he's also an environmental activist, American Indian rights advocate and former C.I.A. recruit. 

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2008/12/weekly-poem-rain-light.html">Weekly Poem: 'Rain Light'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>December 29, 2008</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
W.S. Merwin is counted as one of the nation's greatest living poets. He is the author of more than 50 books of his own poetry, translations of others, memoirs and more.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2008/12/influential-playwright-pinter-dies-at-78.html">Influential Playwright Pinter Dies at 78</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>December 25, 2008</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Harold Pinter, the Nobel Prize-winning playwright who has been lauded as the most influential dramatist of his generation, died Wednesday at age 78 after a long battle with cancer.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2008/12/poetry-at-obamas-inauguration.html">Poetry at Obama's Inauguration</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>December 24, 2008</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
It has been widely noted that President-elect Barack Obama is a reader of poetry. Only days after winning the election, Mr. Obama was spotted with a copy of Derek Walcott's collected poems.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2008/12/conversation-david-thomson-on-film.html">Conversation: David Thomson on Film</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>December 23, 2008</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
For more than 30 years, film critic and scholar David Thomson has been asked one question over and over again: "So, what movies should I see?" His latest book, "Have You Seen....?," is an extended romp of an answer, with short essays on 1,000 films.

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2008/12/your-art-history.html">Weekly Poem: 'Your Art History'</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>December 22, 2008</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Jason Gray is the author of "Photographing Eden" (Ohio Univ. Press, 2008), winner of the Hollis Summers Prize, as well as two chapbooks, "How to Paint the Savior Dead" (Kent State UP, 2007) and "Adam & Eve Go to the Zoo" (Dream Horse, 2003).

       </div>
    </div>
  
    <h3 style="padding-top:10px; margin-bottom:5px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2008/12/conversation-with-alaa-al-aswany.html">Conversation with Alaa al Aswany</a></h3>
    <div style="padding: 0px 10px 15px 0px; border-bottom: dotted 1px #ccc;">
      <div class="comment_form_text"> <strong>December 15, 2008</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
        
Since the release of his first novel, "The Yacoubian Building," in 2002, Alaa al Aswany has catapulted from being a dentist with a literary bent to the Arab-speaking world's best-selling fiction writer.

       </div>
    </div>
  </div> </td>

      <div class="left
        
        ">
        <p style="min-height:35px; margin-bottom:0px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2013/04/weekly-poem-not-a-verbal-equivalent.html">
          <img src="http://newshour.s3.amazonaws.com:80/photos/2013/04/19/dara-wier_video_small.jpg" width="50" height="50" border="0" />

          Weekly Poem: 'Not a Verbal Equivalent'
          </a></p>
      </div>
    
      <div class="
        right
        
        ">
        <p style="min-height:35px; margin-bottom:0px;"><a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/art/blog/2013/04/weekly-poem-child-support-hearing.html">
          <img src="http://newshour.s3.amazonaws.com:80/photos/2013/04/08/nicorvo_video_small.jpeg" width="50" height="50" border="0" />

          Weekly Poem: 'Child Support Hearing'
          </a></p>
      </div>
    
    <div style="clear:both; padding-bottom:0px"></div>
  </div>
